# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0`

# Task: Rename SchedulerProfile to SchedulingProfile

## Objective
Rename `SchedulerProfile` to `SchedulingProfile` in the Kubernetes scheduler
to follow the API naming convention (action-noun pattern).

## Requirements

1. **Rename the type** (likely in scheduler config or profile package):
   - `type SchedulerProfile struct` → `type SchedulingProfile struct`

2. **Update all references** (15+ call sites):
   - `pkg/scheduler/` — scheduler internals
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/` — API types
   - Config and profile loading code
   - Test files

3. **Update constructor functions** and factory methods

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go` — profile definition
- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — uses profiles
- `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/config/` — API config types

## Success Criteria
- `SchedulerProfile` no longer used as type name
- `SchedulingProfile` used instead
- 80%+ of references updated

If an extension point is\\n135: // omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\\n136: // Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\\n137: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\\n138: type Plugins struct {\\n139: \\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\\n140: \\tPreEnqueue PluginSet\\n141: \\n142: \\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\\n143: \\tQueueSort PluginSet\\n144: \\n145: \\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"PreFilter\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n146: \\tPreFilter PluginSet\\n147: \\n148: \\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\\n149: \\tFilter PluginSet\\n150: \\n151: \\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\\n152: \\tPostFilter PluginSet\\n153: \\n154: \\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\\n155: \\tPreScore PluginSet\\n156: \\n157: \\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\\n158: \\tScore PluginSet\\n159: \\n160: \\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\\n161: \\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\\n162: \\tReserve PluginSet\\n163: \\n164: \\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\\n165: \\tPermit PluginSet\\n166: \\n167: \\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\\n168: \\tPreBind PluginSet\\n169: \\n170: \\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"Bind\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n171: \\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\\n172: \\tBind PluginSet\\n173: \\n174: \\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\\n175: \\tPostBind PluginSet\\n176: \\n177: \\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\\n178: \\tMultiPoint PluginSet\\n179: }\\n180: \\n181: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\\n182: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\\n183: type PluginSet struct {\\n184: \\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\\n185: \\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\\n186: \\tEnabled []Plugin\\n187: \\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\\n188: \\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \\\"*\\\" should be provided.\\n189: \\tDisabled []Plugin\\n190: }\\n191: \\n192: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n202: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\\n203: type PluginConfig struct {\\n204: \\t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\\n205: \\tName string\\n206: \\t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n207: \\tArgs runtime.Object\\n208: }\\n209: \\n210: /*\\n211:  * NOTE: The following variables and methods are intentionally left out of the staging mirror.\\n212:  */\\n213: const (\\n214: \\t// DefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore defines the percentage of nodes of all nodes\\n215: \\t// that once found feasible, the scheduler stops looking for more nodes.\\n216: \\t// A value of 0 means adaptive, meaning the scheduler figures out a proper default.\\n217: \\tDefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore = 0\\n218: \\n219: \\t// MaxCustomPriorityScore is the max score UtilizationShapePoint expects.\\n220: \\tMaxCustomPriorityScore int64 = 10\\n221: \\n222: \\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\\n223: \\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\\n224: \\n225: \\t// MaxWeight defines the max weight value allowed for custom PriorityPolicy\\n226: \\tMaxWeight = MaxTotalScore / MaxCustomPriorityScore\\n227: )\\n228: \\n229: // Names returns the list of enabled plugin names.\\n230: func (p *Plugins) Names() []string {\\n231: \\tif p == nil {\\n232: \\t\\treturn nil\\n233: \\t}\\n234: \\textensions := []PluginSet{\\n235: \\t\\tp.PreEnqueue,\\n236: \\t\\tp.PreFilter,\\n237: \\t\\tp.Filter,\\n238: \\t\\tp.PostFilter,\\n239: \\t\\tp.Reserve,\\n240: \\t\\tp.PreScore,\\n241: \\t\\tp.Score,\\n242: \\t\\tp.PreBind,\\n243: \\t\\tp.Bind,\\n244: \\t\\tp.PostBind,\\n245: \\t\\tp.Permit,\\n246: \\t\\tp.QueueSort,\\n247: \\t}\\n248: \\tn := sets.New[string]()\\n249: \\tfor _, e := range extensions {\\n250: \\t\\tfor _, pg := range e.Enabled {\\n251: \\t\\t\\tn.Insert(pg.Name)\\n252: \\t\\t}\\n253: \\t}\\n254: \\treturn sets.List(n)\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\\n265: \\tPreemptVerb string\\n266: \\t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\\n267: \\tPrioritizeVerb string\\n268: \\t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\\n269: \\t// The weight should be a positive integer\\n270: \\tWeight int64\\n271: \\t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. Disabling a plugin through MultiPoint disables that behavior.\\n220: \\t// The same is true for disabling \\\"*\\\" through MultiPoint (no default plugins will be automatically registered).\\n221: \\t// Plugins can still be disabled through their individual extension points.\\n222: \\t//\\n223: \\t// In terms of precedence, plugin config follows this basic hierarchy\\n224: \\t//   1. The set of default plugins, as MultiPoint plugins\\n227: \\t// This implies that a higher precedence plugin will run first and overwrite any settings within MultiPoint.\\n228: \\t// Explicitly user-configured plugins also take a higher precedence over default plugins.\\n229: \\t// Within this hierarchy, an Enabled setting takes precedence over Disabled. For example, if a plugin is\\n230: \\t// set in both `multiPoint.Enabled` and `multiPoint.Disabled`, the plugin will be enabled. Similarly,\\n231: \\t// including `multiPoint.Disabled = '*'` and `multiPoint.Enabled = pluginA` will still register that specific\\n232: \\t// plugin through MultiPoint. This follows the same behavior as all other extension point configurations.\\n233: \\tMultiPoint PluginSet `json:\\\"multiPoint,omitempty\\\"`\\n234: }\\n235: \\n236: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\\n237: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\\n238: type PluginSet struct {\\n239: \\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\\n240: \\t// If the default plugin is also configured in the scheduler config file, the weight of plugin will\\n241: \\t// be overridden accordingly.\\n242: \\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\\n243: \\t// +listType=atomic\\n244: \\tEnabled []Plugin `json:\\\"enabled,omitempty\\\"`\\n245: \\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\\n246: \\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \\\"*\\\" should be provided.\\n247: \\t// +listType=map\\n248: \\t// +listMapKey=name\\n249: \\tDisabled []Plugin `json:\\\"disabled,omitempty\\\"`\\n250: }\\n251: \\n252: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\\n253: type Plugin struct {\\n254: \\t// Name defines the name of plugin\\n255: \\tName string `json:\\\"name\\\"`\\n256: \\t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\\n257: \\tWeight *int32 `json:\\\"weight,omitempty\\\"`\\n258: }\\n259: \\n260: // PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\\n261: // A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n262: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\\n263: type PluginConfig struct {\\n264: \\t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\\n265: \\tName string `json:\\\"name\\\"`\\n266: \\t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\\n267: \\tArgs runtime.RawExtension `json:\\\"args,omitempty\\\"`\\n268: }\\n269: \\n270: func (c *PluginConfig) decodeNestedObjects(d runtime.Decoder) error {\\n271: \\tgvk := SchemeGroupVersion.WithKind(c.Name + \\\"Args\\\")\\n272: \\t// dry-run to detect and skip out-of-tree plugin args.\\n273: \\tif _, _, err := d.Decode(nil, &gvk, nil); runtime.IsNotRegisteredError(err) {\\n274: \\t\\treturn nil\\n275: \\t}\\n276: \\n277: \\tvar strictDecodingErr error\\n278: \\tobj, parsedGvk, err := d.Decode(c.Args.Raw, &gvk, nil)\\n279: \\tif err != nil {\\n280: \\t\\tdecodingArgsErr := fmt.Errorf(\\\"decoding args for plugin %s: %w\\\", c.Name, err)\\n281: \\t\\tif obj != nil && runtime.IsStrictDecodingError(err) {\\n282: \\t\\t\\tstrictDecodingErr = runtime.NewStrictDecodingError([]error{decodingArgsErr})\\n283: \\t\\t} else {\\n284: \\t\\t\\treturn decodingArgsErr\\n285: \\t\\t}\\n286: \\t}\\n287: \\tif parsedGvk.GroupKind() != gvk.GroupKind() {\\n288: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"args for plugin %s were not of type %s, got %s\\\", c.Name, gvk.GroupKind(), parsedGvk.GroupKind())\\n289: \\t}\\n290: \\tc.Args.Object = obj\\n291: \\treturn strictDecodingErr\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: func (c *PluginConfig) encodeNestedObjects(e runtime.Encoder) error {\\n295: \\tif c.Args.Object == nil {\\n296: \\t\\treturn nil\\n297: \\t}\\n298: \\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\\n299: \\terr := e.Encode(c.Args.Object, &buf)\\n300: \\tif err != nil {\\n301: \\t\\treturn err\\n302: \\t}\\n303: \\t// The <e> encoder might be a YAML encoder, but the parent encoder expects\\n304: \\t// JSON output, so we convert YAML back to JSON.\\n305: \\t// This is a no-op if <e> produces JSON.\\n306: \\tjson, err := yaml.YAMLToJSON(buf.Bytes())\\n307: \\tif err != nil {\\n308: \\t\\treturn err\\n309: \\t}\\n310: \\tc.Args.Raw = json\\n311: \\treturn nil\\n312: }\\n313: \\n314: // Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. If a verb is unspecified/empty,\\n315: // it is assumed that the extender chose not to provide that extension.\\n316: type Extender struct {\\n317: \\t// URLPrefix at which the extender is available\\n318: \\tURLPrefix string `json:\\\"urlPrefix\\\"`\\n319: \\t// Verb for the filter call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the filter call to extender.\\n320: \\tFilterVerb string `json:\\\"filterVerb,omitempty\\\"`\\n321: \\t// Verb for the preempt call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\\n322: \\tPreemptVerb string `json:\\\"preemptVerb,omitempty\\\"`\\n323: \\t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\\n324: \\tPrioritizeVerb string `json:\\\"prioritizeVerb,omitempty\\\"`\\n325: \\t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\\n326: \\t// The weight should be a positive integer\\n327: \\tWeight int64 `json:\\\"weight,omitempty\\\"`\\n328: \\t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the bind call to extender.\\n329: \\t// If this method is implemented by the extender, it is the extender's responsibility to bind the pod to apiserver. Only one extender\\n330: \\t// can implement this function.\\n331: \\tBindVerb string `json:\\\"bindVerb,omitempty\\\"`\\n332: \\t// EnableHTTPS specifies whether https should be used to communicate with the extender\\n333: \\tEnableHTTPS bool `json:\\\"enableHTTPS,omitempty\\\"`\\n334: \\t// TLSConfig specifies the transport layer security config\\n335: \\tTLSConfig *ExtenderTLSConfig `json:\\\"tlsConfig,omitempty\\\"`\\n336: \\t// HTTPTimeout specifies the timeout duration for a call to the extender. Filter timeout fails the scheduling of the pod. Prioritize\\n337: \\t// timeout is ignored, k8s/other extenders priorities are used to select the node.\\n338: \\tHTTPTimeout metav1.Duration `json:\\\"httpTimeout,omitempty\\\"`\\n339: \\t// NodeCacheCapable specifies that the extender is capable of caching node information,\\n340: \\t// so the scheduler should only send minimal information about the eligible nodes\\n341: \\t// assuming that the extender already cached full details of all nodes in the cluster\\n342: \\tNodeCacheCapable bool `json:\\\"nodeCacheCapable,omitempty\\\"`\\n343: \\t// ManagedResources is a list of extended resources that are managed by\\n344: \\t// this extender.\\n345: \\t// - A pod will be sent to the extender on the Filter, Prioritize and Bind\\n346: \\t//   (if the extender is the binder) phases iff the pod requests at least\\n347: \\t//   one of the extended resources in this list. If it is empty,\n152: \t// global PercentageOfNodesToScore will be used.\n153: \tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32 `json:\"percentageOfNodesToScore,omitempty\"`\n154: \n155: \t// Plugins specify the set of plugins that should be enabled or disabled.\n156: \t// Enabled plugins are the ones that should be enabled in addition to the\n157: \t// default plugins. Disabled plugins are any of the default plugins that\n158: \t// should be disabled.\n159: \t// When no enabled or disabled plugin is specified for an extension point,\n160: \t// default plugins for that extension point will be used if there is any.\n161: \t// If a QueueSort plugin is specified, the same QueueSort Plugin and\n162: \t// PluginConfig must be specified for all profiles.\n163: \tPlugins *Plugins `json:\"plugins,omitempty\"`\n164: \n165: \t// PluginConfig is an optional set of custom plugin arguments for each plugin.\n166: \t// Omitting config args for a plugin is equivalent to using the default config\n167: \t// for that plugin.\n168: \t// +listType=map\n169: \t// +listMapKey=name\n170: \tPluginConfig []PluginConfig `json:\"pluginConfig,omitempty\"`\n171: }\n172: \n173: // Plugins include multiple extension points. When specified, the list of plugins for\n174: // a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\n175: // omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\n176: // Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\n177: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\n178: type Plugins struct {\n179: \t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\n180: \tPreEnqueue PluginSet `json:\"preEnqueue,omitempty\"`\n181: \n182: \t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\n183: \tQueueSort PluginSet `json:\"queueSort,omitempty\"`\n184: \n185: \t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"PreFilter\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n186: \tPreFilter PluginSet `json:\"preFilter,omitempty\"`\n187: \n188: \t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\n189: \tFilter PluginSet `json:\"filter,omitempty\"`\n190: \n191: \t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\n192: \tPostFilter PluginSet `json:\"postFilter,omitempty\"`\n193: \n194: \t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\n195: \tPreScore PluginSet `json:\"preScore,omitempty\"`\n196: \n197: \t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\n198: \tScore PluginSet `json:\"score,omitempty\"`\n199: \n200: \t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\n201: \t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\n202: \tReserve PluginSet `json:\"reserve,omitempty\"`\n203: \n204: \t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\n205: \tPermit PluginSet `json:\"permit,omitempty\"`\n206: \n207: \t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\n208: \tPreBind PluginSet `json:\"preBind,omitempty\"`\n209: \n210: \t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"Bind\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n211: \t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n212: \tBind PluginSet `json:\"bind,omitempty\"`\n213: \n214: \t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n215: \tPostBind PluginSet `json:\"postBind,omitempty\"`\n216: \n217: \t// MultiPoint is a simplified config section to enable plugins for all valid extension points.\n218: \t// Plugins enabled through MultiPoint will automatically register for every individual extension\n219: \t// point the plugin has implemented. Disabling a plugin through MultiPoint disables that behavior.\n220: \t// The same is true for disabling \"*\" through MultiPoint (no default plugins will be automatically registered).\n221: \t// Plugins can still be disabled through their individual extension points.\n222: \t//\n223: \t// In terms of precedence, plugin config follows this basic hierarchy\n224: \t//   1. Specific extension points\n225: \t//   2. Explicitly configured MultiPoint plugins\n226: \t//   3. The set of default plugins, as MultiPoint plugins\n227: \t// This implies that a higher precedence plugin will run first and overwrite any settings within MultiPoint.\n228: \t// Explicitly user-configured plugins also take a higher precedence over default plugins.\n229: \t// Within this hierarchy, an Enabled setting takes precedence over Disabled. For example, if a plugin is\n230: \t// set in both `multiPoint.Enabled` and `multiPoint.Disabled`, the plugin will be enabled. Similarly,\n231: \t// including `multiPoint.Disabled = '*'` and `multiPoint.Enabled = pluginA` will still register that specific\n232: \t// plugin through MultiPoint. This follows the same behavior as all other extension point configurations.\n233: \tMultiPoint PluginSet `json:\"multiPoint,omitempty\"`\n234: }\n235: \n236: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\n237: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\n238: type PluginSet struct {\n239: \t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\n240: \t// If the default plugin is also configured in the scheduler config file, the weight of plugin will\n241: \t// be overridden accordingly.\n242: \t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\n243: \t// +listType=atomic\n244: \tEnabled []Plugin `json:\"enabled,omitempty\"`\n245: \t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\n246: \t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \"*\" should be provided.\n247: \t// +listType=map\n248: \t// +listMapKey=name\n249: \tDisabled []Plugin `json:\"disabled,omitempty\"`\n250: }\n251: \n252: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\n253: type Plugin struct {\n254: \t// Name defines the name of plugin\n255: \tName string `json:\"name\"`\n256: \t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\n257: \tWeight *int32 `json:\"weight,omitempty\"`\n258: }\n259: \n260: // PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\n261: // A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n262: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\n263: type PluginConfig struct {\n264: \t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\n265: \tName string `json:\"name\"`\n266: \t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n267: \tArgs runtime.RawExtension `json:\"args,omitempty\"`\n268: }\n269: \n270: func (c *PluginConfig) decodeNestedObjects(d runtime.Decoder) error {\n271: \tgvk := SchemeGroupVersion.WithKind(c.Name + \"Args\")\n272: \t// dry-run to detect and skip out-of-tree plugin args.\n273: \tif _, _, err := d.Decode(nil, &gvk, nil); runtime.IsNotRegisteredError(err) {\n274: \t\treturn nil\n275: \t}\n276: \n277: \tvar strictDecodingErr error\n278: \tobj, parsedGvk, err := d.Decode(c.Args.Raw, &gvk, nil)\n279: \tif err != nil {\n280: \t\tdecodingArgsErr := fmt.Errorf(\"decoding args for plugin %s: %w\", c.Name, err)\n281: \t\tif obj != nil && runtime.IsStrictDecodingError(err) {\n282: \t\t\tstrictDecodingErr = runtime.NewStrictDecodingError([]error{decodingArgsErr})\n283: \t\t} else {\n284: \t\t\treturn decodingArgsErr\n285: \t\t}\n286: \t}\n287: \tif parsedGvk.GroupKind() != gvk.GroupKind() {\n288: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"args for plugin %s were not of type %s, got %s\", c.Name, gvk.GroupKind(), parsedGvk.GroupKind())\n289: \t}\n290: \tc.Args.Object = obj\n291: \treturn strictDecodingErr\n292: }\n293: \n294: func (c *PluginConfig) encodeNestedObjects(e runtime.Encoder) error {\n295: \tif c.Args.Object == nil {\n296: \t\treturn nil\n297: \t}\n298: \tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n299: \terr := e.Encode(c.Args.Object, &buf)\n300: \tif err != nil {\n301: \t\treturn err\n302: \t}\n303: \t// The <e> encoder might be a YAML encoder, but the parent encoder expects\n304: \t// JSON output, so we convert YAML back to JSON.\n305: \t// This is a no-op if <e> produces JSON.\n306: \tjson, err := yaml.YAMLToJSON(buf.Bytes())\n307: \tif err != nil {\n308: \t\treturn err\n309: \t}\n310: \tc.Args.Raw = json\n311: \treturn nil\n312: }\n313: \n314: // Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. If a verb is unspecified/empty,\n315: // it is assumed that the extender chose not to provide that extension.\n316: type Extender struct {\n317: \t// URLPrefix at which the extender is available\n318: \tURLPrefix string `json:\"urlPrefix\"`\n319: \t// Verb for the filter call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the filter call to extender.\n320: \tFilterVerb string `json:\"filterVerb,omitempty\"`\n321: \t// Verb for the preempt call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\n322: \tPreemptVerb string `json:\"preemptVerb,omitempty\"`\n323: \t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\n324: \tPrioritizeVerb string `json:\"prioritizeVerb,omitempty\"`\n325: \t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\n326: \t// The weight should be a positive integer\n327: \tWeight int64 `json:\"weight,omitempty\"`\n328: \t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the bind call to extender.\n329: \t// If this method is implemented by the extender, it is the extender's responsibility to bind the pod to apiserver. Only one extender\n330: \t// can implement this function.\n331: \tBindVerb string `json:\"bindVerb,omitempty\"`\n332: \t// EnableHTTPS specifies whether https should be used to communicate with the extender\n333: \tEnableHTTPS bool `json:\"enableHTTPS,omitempty\"`\n334: \t// TLSConfig specifies the transport layer security config\n335: \tTLSConfig *ExtenderTLSConfig `json:\"tlsConfig,omitempty\"`\n336: \t// HTTPTimeout specifies the timeout duration for a call to the extender. }\n371: \n372: func buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\n373: \tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n374: \tfor _, e := range es {\n375: \t\tevents := e.EventsToRegister()\n376: \n377: \t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n378: \t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n379: \t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n380: \t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n381: \t\t\tcontinue\n382: \t\t}\n383: \n384: \t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n385: \t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n386: \t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n387: \t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n388: \n389: \t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n390: \t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n391: \t\tfor _, event := range events {\n392: \t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n393: \t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n394: \t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n395: \t\t\t}\n396: \n397: \t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n398: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n399: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n400: \t\t\t\t}\n401: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n402: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n403: \t\t\t\t}\n404: \t\t\t}\n405: \n406: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n407: \t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n408: \t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n409: \t\t\t})\n410: \t\t}\n411: \t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n412: \t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n413: \t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n414: \t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n415: \t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n416: \t\t\t//\n417: \t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n418: \t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n419: \t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n420: \t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n421: \t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n422: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n423: \t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n424: \t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n425: \t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n426: \t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n427: \t\t\t\t\t},\n428: \t\t\t\t)\n429: \t\t}\n430: \t}\n431: \treturn queueingHintMap\n432: }\n433: \n434: // Run begins watching and scheduling. It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\n435: func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n436: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n437: \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n438: \n439: \t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n440: \t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n441: \t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n442: \t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n443: \t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n444: \t// SchedulingQueue, in effect causing a deadlock on shutdown.\n445: \tgo wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n446: \n447: \t<-ctx.Done()\n448: \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Close()\n449: \n450: \t// If the plugins satisfy the io.Closer interface, they are closed.\n451: \terr := sched.Profiles.Close()\n452: \tif err != nil {\n453: \t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to close plugins\")\n454: \t}\n455: }\n456: \n457: // NewInformerFactory creates a SharedInformerFactory and initializes a scheduler specific\n458: // in-place podInformer.\n459: func NewInformerFactory(cs clientset.Interface, resyncPeriod \treturn informerFactory\n463: }\n464: \n465: func buildExtenders(logger klog.Logger, extenders []schedulerapi.Extender, profiles []schedulerapi.KubeSchedulerProfile) ([]framework.Extender, error) {\n466: \tvar fExtenders []framework.Extender\n467: \tif len(extenders) == 0 {\n468: \t\treturn nil, nil\n469: \t}\n470: \n471: \tvar ignoredExtendedResources []string\n472: \tvar ignorableExtenders \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\tif !extender.IsIgnorable() {\n480: \t\t\tfExtenders = append(fExtenders, extender)\n481: \t\t} else {\n482: \t\t\tignorableExtenders = append(ignorableExtenders, extender)\n483: \t\t}\n484: \t\tfor _, r := range extenders[i].ManagedResources {\n485: \t\t\tif r.IgnoredByScheduler {\n486: \t\t\t\tignoredExtendedResources = append(ignoredExtendedResources, r.Name)\n487: \t\t\t}\n488: \t\t}\n489: \t}\n490: \t// place ignorable extenders to the tail of extenders\n491: \tfExtenders = append(fExtenders, ignorableExtenders...)\n492: \n493: \t// If there are any extended resources found from the Extenders, append them to the pluginConfig for each profile.\n494: \t// This should only have an effect on ComponentConfig, where it is possible to configure Extenders and\n495: \t// plugin args (and in which case the extender ignored resources take precedence).\n496: \tif len(ignoredExtendedResources) == 0 {\n497: \t\treturn fExtenders, nil\n498: \t}\n499: \n500: \tfor i := range profiles {\n501: \t\tprof := &profiles[i]\n502: \t\tvar found = false\n503: \t\tfor k := range prof.PluginConfig {\n504: \t\t\tif prof.PluginConfig[k].Name == noderesources.Name {\n505: \t\t\t\t// Update the existing args\n506: \t\t\t\tpc := &prof.PluginConfig[k]\n507: \t\t\t\targs, ok := pc.Args.(*schedulerapi.NodeResourcesFitArgs)\n508: \t\t\t\tif !ok {\n509: \t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"want args to be of type NodeResourcesFitArgs, got %T\", pc.Args)\n510: \t\t\t\t}\n511: \t\t\t\targs.IgnoredResources = ignoredExtendedResources\n512: \t\t\t\tfound = true\n513: \t\t\t\tbreak\n514: \t\t\t}\n515: \t\t}\n516: \t\tif !found {\n517: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"can't find NodeResourcesFitArgs in plugin config\")\n518: \t\t}\n519: \t}\n520: \treturn fExtenders, nil\n521: }\n522: \n523: type FailureHandlerFn func(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo, status *framework.Status, nominatingInfo *framework.NominatingInfo, start time.Time)\n524: \n525: func unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile If they need to\n137: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\n138: type Plugins struct {\n139: \t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\n140: \tPreEnqueue PluginSet\n141: \n142: \t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\n143: \tQueueSort PluginSet\n144: \n145: \t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"PreFilter\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n146: \tPreFilter PluginSet\n147: \n148: \t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\n149: \tFilter PluginSet\n150: \n151: \t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\n152: \tPostFilter PluginSet\n153: \n154: \t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\n155: \tPreScore PluginSet\n156: \n157: \t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\n158: \tScore PluginSet\n159: \n160: \t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\n161: \t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\n162: \tReserve PluginSet\n163: \n164: \t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\n165: \tPermit PluginSet\n166: \n167: \t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\n168: \tPreBind PluginSet\n169: \n170: \t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"Bind\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n171: \t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n172: \tBind PluginSet\n173: \n174: \t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n175: \tPostBind PluginSet\n176: \n177: \t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\n178: \tMultiPoint PluginSet\n179: }\n180: \n181: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\n182: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\n183: type PluginSet struct {\n184: \t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\n185: \t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\n186: \tEnabled []Plugin\n187: \t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\n188: \t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \"*\" should be provided.\n189: \tDisabled []Plugin\n190: }\n191: \n192: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\n193: type Plugin struct {\n194: \t// Name defines the name of plugin\n195: \tName string\n196: \t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\n197: \tWeight int32\n198: }\n199: \n200: // PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\n201: // A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n202: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\n203: type PluginConfig struct {\n204: \t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\n205: \tName string\n206: \t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n207: \tArgs runtime.Object\n208: }\n209: \n210: /*\n211:  * NOTE: The following variables and methods are intentionally left out of the staging mirror.\n212:  */\n213: const (\n214: \t// DefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore defines the percentage of nodes of all nodes\n215: \t// that once found feasible, the scheduler stops looking for more nodes.\n216: \t// A value of 0 means adaptive, meaning the scheduler figures out a proper default.\n217: \tDefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore = 0\n218: \n219: \t// MaxCustomPriorityScore is the max score UtilizationShapePoint expects.\n220: \tMaxCustomPriorityScore int64 = 10\n221: \n222: \t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n223: \tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n224: \n225: \t// MaxWeight defines the max weight value allowed for custom PriorityPolicy\n226: \tMaxWeight = MaxTotalScore / MaxCustomPriorityScore\n227: )\n228: \n229: // Names returns the list of enabled plugin names.\n230: func (p *Plugins) Names() []string {\n231: \tif p == nil {\n232: \t\treturn nil\n233: \t}\n234: \textensions := []PluginSet{\n235: \t\tp.PreEnqueue,\n236: \t\tp.PreFilter,\n237: \t\tp.Filter,\n238: \t\tp.PostFilter,\n239: \t\tp.Reserve,\n240: \t\tp.PreScore,\n241: \t\tp.Score,\n242: \t\tp.PreBind,\n243: \t\tp.Bind,\n244: \t\tp.PostBind,\n245: \t\tp.Permit,\n246: \t\tp.QueueSort,\n247: \t}\n248: \tn := sets.New[string]()\n249: \tfor _, e := range extensions {\n250: \t\tfor _, pg := range e.Enabled {\n251: \t\t\tn.Insert(pg.Name)\n252: \t\t}\n253: \t}\n254: \treturn sets.List(n)\n255: }\n256: \n257: // Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. If a verb is unspecified/empty,\n258: // it is assumed that the extender chose not to provide that extension.\n259: type Extender struct {\n260: \t// URLPrefix at which the extender is available\n261: \tURLPrefix string\n262: \t// Verb for the filter call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the filter call to extender.\n263: \tFilterVerb string\n264: \t// Verb for the preempt call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\n265: \tPreemptVerb string\n266: \t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\n267: \tPrioritizeVerb string\n268: \t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\n269: \t// The weight should be a positive integer\n270: \tWeight int64\n271: \t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. In kube-scheduler, after\n\t// conversion from the versioned KubeSchedulerConfiguration type to this\n\t// internal type, we set the APIVersion field to the scheme group/version of\n\t// the type we converted from. This is done in cmd/kube-scheduler in two\n\t// places: (1) when loading config from a file, (2) generating the default\n\t// config. Based on the versioned type set in this field, we make decisions;\n\t// for example (1) during validation to check for usage of removed plugins,\n\t// (2) writing config to a file, (3) initialising the scheduler.\n\tmetav1.TypeMeta\n\n\t// Parallelism defines the amount of parallelism in algorithms for scheduling a Pods. Must be greater than 0. Defaults to 16\n\tParallelism int32\n\n\t// LeaderElection defines the configuration of leader election client.\n\tLeaderElection componentbaseconfig.LeaderElectionConfiguration\n\n\t// ClientConnection specifies the kubeconfig file and client connection\n\t// settings for the proxy server to use when communicating with the apiserver.\n\tClientConnection componentbaseconfig.ClientConnectionConfiguration\n\n\t// DebuggingConfiguration holds configuration for Debugging related features\n\t// TODO: We might wanna make this a substruct like Debugging componentbaseconfig.DebuggingConfiguration\n\tcomponentbaseconfig.DebuggingConfiguration\n\n\t// PercentageOfNodesToScore is the percentage of all nodes that once found feasible\n\t// for running a pod, the scheduler stops its search for more feasible nodes in\n\t// the cluster. This helps improve scheduler's performance. Scheduler always tries to find\n\t// at least \"minFeasibleNodesToFind\" feasible nodes no matter what the value of this flag is.\n\t// Example: if the cluster size is 500 nodes and the value of this flag is 30,\n\t// then scheduler stops finding further feasible nodes once it finds 150 feasible ones.\n\t// When the value is 0, default percentage (5%--50% based on the size of the cluster) of the\n\t// nodes will be scored. It is overridden by profile level PercentageOfNodesToScore.\n\tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32\n\n\t// PodInitialBackoffSeconds is the initial backoff for unschedulable pods.\n\t// If specified, it must be greater than 0. If this value is null, the default value (1s)\n\t// will be used.\n\tPodInitialBackoffSeconds int64\n\n\t// PodMaxBackoffSeconds is the max backoff for unschedulable pods.\n\t// If specified, it must be greater than or equal to podInitialBackoffSeconds. If this value is null,\n\t// the default value (10s) will be used.\n\tPodMaxBackoffSeconds int64\n\n\t// Profiles are scheduling profiles that kube-scheduler supports. Pods can\n\t// choose to be scheduled under a particular profile by setting its associated\n\t// scheduler name. Pods that don't specify any scheduler name are scheduled\n\t// with the \"default-scheduler\" profile, if present here.\n\tProfiles []KubeSchedulingProfile\n\n\t// Extenders are the list of scheduler extenders, each holding the values of how to communicate\n\t// with the extender. These extenders are shared by all scheduler profiles.\n\tExtenders []Extender\n\n\t// DelayCacheUntilActive specifies when to start caching. If this is true and leader election is enabled,\n\t// the scheduler will wait to fill informer caches until it is the leader. Doing so will have slower\n\t// failover with the benefit of lower memory overhead while waiting to become leader.\n\t// Defaults to false.\n\tDelayCacheUntilActive bool\n}\n\n// KubeSchedulingProfile is a scheduling profile.\ntype KubeSchedulingProfile struct {\n\t// SchedulerName is the name of the scheduler associated to this profile.\n\t// If SchedulerName matches with the pod's \"spec.schedulerName\", then the pod\n\t// is scheduled with this profile.\n\tSchedulerName string\n\n\t// PercentageOfNodesToScore is the percentage of all nodes that once found feasible\n\t// for running a pod, the scheduler stops its search for more feasible nodes in\n\t// the cluster. This helps improve scheduler's performance. Scheduler always tries to find\n\t// at least \"minFeasibleNodesToFind\" feasible nodes no matter what the value of this flag is.\n\t// Example: if the cluster size is 500 nodes and the value of this flag is 30,\n\t// then scheduler stops finding further feasible nodes once it finds 150 feasible ones.\n\t// When the value is 0, default percentage (5%--50% based on the size of the cluster) of the\n\t// nodes will be scored. It will override global PercentageOfNodesToScore. If it is empty,\n\t// global PercentageOfNodesToScore will be used.\n\tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32\n\n\t// Plugins specify the set of plugins that should be enabled or disabled.\n\t// Enabled plugins are the ones that should be enabled in addition to the\n\t// default plugins. Disabled plugins are any of the default plugins that\n\t// should be disabled.\n\t// When no enabled or disabled plugin is specified for an extension point,\n\t// default plugins for that extension point will be used if there is any.\n\t// If a QueueSort plugin is specified, the same QueueSort Plugin and\n\t// PluginConfig must be specified for all profiles.\n\tPlugins *Plugins\n\n\t// PluginConfig is an optional set of custom plugin arguments for each plugin.\n\t// Omitting config args for a plugin is equivalent to using the default config\n\t// for that plugin.\n\tPluginConfig []PluginConfig\n}\n\n// Plugins include multiple extension points. When specified, the list of plugins for\n// a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\n// omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\n// Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\n// be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\ntype Plugins struct {\n\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\n\tPreEnqueue PluginSet\n\n\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\n\tQueueSort PluginSet\n\n\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"PreFilter\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n\tPreFilter PluginSet\n\n\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\n\tFilter PluginSet\n\n\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\n\tPostFilter PluginSet\n\n\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\n\tPreScore PluginSet\n\n\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\n\tScore PluginSet\n\n\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\n\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\n\tReserve PluginSet\n\n\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\n\tPermit PluginSet\n\n\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\n\tPreBind PluginSet\n\n\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"Bind\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n\tBind PluginSet\n\n\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n\tPostBind PluginSet\n\n\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\n\tMultiPoint PluginSet\n}\n\n// PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\n// If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\ntype PluginSet struct {\n\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\n\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\n\tEnabled []Plugin\n\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\n\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \"*\" should be provided.\n\tDisabled []Plugin\n}\n\n// Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\ntype Plugin struct {\n\t// Name defines the name of plugin\n\tName string\n\t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\n\tWeight int32\n}\n\n// PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\n// A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n// It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\ntype PluginConfig struct {\n\t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\n\tName string\n\t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n\tArgs runtime.Object\n}\n\n/*\n * NOTE: The following variables and methods are intentionally left out of the staging mirror.\n */\nconst (\n\t// DefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore defines the percentage of nodes of all nodes\n\t// that once found feasible, the scheduler stops looking for more nodes.\n\t// A value of 0 means adaptive, meaning the scheduler figures out a proper default.\n\tDefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore = 0\n\n\t// MaxCustomPriorityScore is the max score UtilizationShapePoint expects.\n\tMaxCustomPriorityScore int64 = 10\n\n\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n\n\t// MaxWeight defines the max weight value allowed for custom PriorityPolicy\n\tMaxWeight = MaxTotalScore / MaxCustomPriorityScore\n)\n\n// Names returns the list of enabled plugin names.\nfunc (p *Plugins) Names() []string {\n\tif p == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\textensions := []PluginSet{\n\t\tp.PreEnqueue,\n\t\tp.PreFilter,\n\t\tp.Filter,\n\t\tp.PostFilter,\n\t\tp.Reserve,\n\t\tp.PreScore,\n\t\tp.Score,\n\t\tp.PreBind,\n\t\tp.Bind,\n\t\tp.PostBind,\n\t\tp.Permit,\n\t\tp.QueueSort,\n\t}\n\tn := sets.New[string]()\n\tfor _, e := range extensions {\n\t\tfor _, pg := range e.Enabled {\n\t\t\tn.Insert(pg.Name)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn sets.List(n)\n}\n\n// Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. If a verb is unspecified/empty,\n// it is assumed that the extender chose not to provide that extension.\ntype Extender struct {\n\t// URLPrefix at which the extender is available\n\tURLPrefix string\n\t// Verb for the filter call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the filter call to extender.\n\tFilterVerb string\n\t// Verb for the preempt call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\n\tPreemptVerb string\n\t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\n\tPrioritizeVerb string\n\t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\n\t// The weight should be a positive integer\n\tWeight int64\n\t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the bind call to extender.\n\t// If this method is implemented by the extender, it is the extender's responsibility to bind the pod to apiserver. Only one extender\n\t// can implement this function.\n\tBindVerb string\n\t// EnableHTTPS specifies whether https should be used to communicate with the extender\n\tEnableHTTPS bool\n\t// TLSConfig specifies the transport layer security config\n\tTLSConfig *ExtenderTLSConfig\n\t// HTTPTimeout specifies the timeout duration for a call to the extender. Filter timeout fails the scheduling of the pod. Prioritize\n\t// timeout is ignored, k8s/other extenders priorities are used to select the node.\n\tHTTPTimeout metav1.Duration\n\t// NodeCacheCapable specifies that the extender is capable of caching node information,\n\t// so the scheduler should only send minimal information about the eligible nodes\n\t// assuming that the extender already cached full details of all nodes in the cluster\n\tNodeCacheCapable bool\n\t// ManagedResources is a list of extended resources that are managed by\n\t// this extender.\n\t// - A pod will be sent to the extender on the Filter, Prioritize and Bind\n\t//   (if the extender is the binder) phases iff the pod requests at least\n\t//   one of the extended resources in this list. If empty or unspecified,\n\t//   all pods will be sent to this extender.\n\t// - If IgnoredByScheduler is set to true for a resource, kube-scheduler\n\t//   will skip checking the resource in predicates.\n\t// +optional\n\tManagedResources []ExtenderManagedResource\n\t// Ignorable specifies if the extender is ignorable, i.e. scheduling should not\n\t// fail when the extender returns an error or is not reachable.\n\tIgnorable bool\n}\n\n// ExtenderManagedResource describes the arguments of extended resources\n// managed by an extender.\ntype ExtenderManagedResource struct {\n\t// Name is the extended resource name.\n\tName string\n\t// IgnoredByScheduler indicates whether kube-scheduler should ignore this\n\t// resource when applying predicates.\n\tIgnoredByScheduler bool\n}\n\n// ExtenderTLSConfig contains settings to enable TLS with extender\ntype ExtenderTLSConfig struct {\n\t// Server should be accessed without verifying the TLS certificate. For testing only.\n\tInsecure bool\n\t// ServerName is passed to the server for SNI and is used in the client to check server\n\t// certificates against. If ServerName is empty, the hostname used to contact the\n\t// server is used.\n\tServerName string\n\n\t// Server requires TLS client certificate authentication\n\tCertFile string\n\t// Server requires TLS client certificate authentication\n\tKeyFile string\n\t// Trusted root certificates for server\n\tCAFile string\n\n\t// CertData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a client certificate file).\n\t// CertData takes precedence over CertFile\n\tCertData []byte\n\t// KeyData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a client certificate key file).\n\t// KeyData takes precedence over KeyFile\n\tKeyData []byte `datapolicy:\"security-key\"`\n\t// CAData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a root certificates bundle).\n\t// CAData takes precedence over CAFile\n\tCAData []byte\n}\n",

Defaults to 16\n\tParallelism *int32 `json:\"parallelism,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// LeaderElection defines the configuration of leader election client.\n\tLeaderElection componentbaseconfigv1alpha1.LeaderElectionConfiguration `json:\"leaderElection\"`\n\n\t// ClientConnection specifies the kubeconfig file and client connection\n\t// settings for the proxy server to use when communicating with the apiserver.\n\tClientConnection componentbaseconfigv1alpha1.ClientConnectionConfiguration `json:\"clientConnection\"`\n\n\t// DebuggingConfiguration holds configuration for Debugging related features\n\t// TODO: We might wanna make this a substruct like Debugging componentbaseconfigv1alpha1.DebuggingConfiguration\n\tcomponentbaseconfigv1alpha1.DebuggingConfiguration `json:\",inline\"`\n\n\t// PercentageOfNodesToScore is the percentage of all nodes that once found feasible\n\t// for running a pod, the scheduler stops its search for more feasible nodes in\n\t// the cluster. This helps improve scheduler's performance. Scheduler always tries to find\n\t// at least \"minFeasibleNodesToFind\" feasible nodes no matter what the value of this flag is.\n\t// Example: if the cluster size is 500 nodes and the value of this flag is 30,\n\t// then scheduler stops finding further feasible nodes once it finds 150 feasible ones.\n\t// When the value is 0, default percentage (5%--50% based on the size of the cluster) of the\n\t// nodes will be scored. It is overridden by profile level PercentageofNodesToScore.\n\tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32 `json:\"percentageOfNodesToScore,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PodInitialBackoffSeconds is the initial backoff for unschedulable pods.\n\t// If specified, it must be greater than 0. If this value is null, the default value (1s)\n\t// will be used.\n\tPodInitialBackoffSeconds *int64 `json:\"podInitialBackoffSeconds,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PodMaxBackoffSeconds is the max backoff for unschedulable pods.\n\t// If specified, it must be greater than podInitialBackoffSeconds. If this value is null,\n\t// the default value (10s) will be used.\n\tPodMaxBackoffSeconds *int64 `json:\"podMaxBackoffSeconds,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Profiles are scheduling profiles that kube-scheduler supports. Pods can\n\t// choose to be scheduled under a particular profile by setting its associated\n\t// scheduler name. Pods that don't specify any scheduler name are scheduled\n\t// with the \"default-scheduler\" profile, if present here.\n\t// +listType=map\n\t// +listMapKey=schedulerName\n\tProfiles []KubeSchedulingProfile `json:\"profiles,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Extenders are the list of scheduler extenders, each holding the values of how to communicate\n\t// with the extender. These extenders are shared by all scheduler profiles.\n\t// +listType=set\n\tExtenders []Extender `json:\"extenders,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// DelayCacheUntilActive specifies when to start caching. If this is true and leader election is enabled,\n\t// the scheduler will wait to fill informer caches until it is the leader. Doing so will have slower\n\t// failover with the benefit of lower memory overhead while waiting to become leader.\n\t// Defaults to false.\n\tDelayCacheUntilActive bool `json:\"delayCacheUntilActive,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// DecodeNestedObjects decodes plugin args for known types.\nfunc (c *KubeSchedulerConfiguration) DecodeNestedObjects(d runtime.Decoder) error {\n\tvar strictDecodingErrs []error\n\tfor i := range c.Profiles {\n\t\tprof := &c.Profiles[i]\n\t\tfor j := range prof.PluginConfig {\n\t\t\terr := prof.PluginConfig[j].decodeNestedObjects(d)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tdecodingErr := fmt.Errorf(\"decoding .profiles[%d].pluginConfig[%d]: %w\", i, j, err)\n\t\t\t\tif runtime.IsStrictDecodingError(err) {\n\t\t\t\t\tstrictDecodingErrs = append(strictDecodingErrs, decodingErr)\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn decodingErr\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(strictDecodingErrs) > 0 {\n\t\treturn runtime.NewStrictDecodingError(strictDecodingErrs)\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// EncodeNestedObjects encodes plugin args.\nfunc (c *KubeSchedulerConfiguration) EncodeNestedObjects(e runtime.Encoder) error {\n\tfor i := range c.Profiles {\n\t\tprof := &c.Profiles[i]\n\t\tfor j := range prof.PluginConfig {\n\t\t\terr := prof.PluginConfig[j].encodeNestedObjects(e)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"encoding .profiles[%d].pluginConfig[%d]: %w\", i, j, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// KubeSchedulingProfile is a scheduling profile.\ntype KubeSchedulingProfile struct {\n\t// SchedulerName is the name of the scheduler associated to this profile.\n\t// If SchedulerName matches with the pod's \"spec.schedulerName\", then the pod\n\t// is scheduled with this profile.\n\tSchedulerName *string `json:\"schedulerName,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PercentageOfNodesToScore is the percentage of all nodes that once found feasible\n\t// for running a pod, the scheduler stops its search for more feasible nodes in\n\t// the cluster. This helps improve scheduler's performance. Scheduler always tries to find\n\t// at least \"minFeasibleNodesToFind\" feasible nodes no matter what the value of this flag is.\n\t// Example: if the cluster size is 500 nodes and the value of this flag is 30,\n\t// then scheduler stops finding further feasible nodes once it finds 150 feasible ones.\n\t// When the value is 0, default percentage (5%--50% based on the size of the cluster) of the\n\t// nodes will be scored. It will override global PercentageOfNodesToScore. If it is empty,\n\t// global PercentageOfNodesToScore will be used.\n\tPercentageOfNodesToScore *int32 `json:\"percentageOfNodesToScore,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Plugins specify the set of plugins that should be enabled or disabled.\n\t// Enabled plugins are the ones that should be enabled in addition to the\n\t// default plugins. Disabled plugins are any of the default plugins that\n\t// should be disabled.\n\t// When no enabled or disabled plugin is specified for an extension point,\n\t// default plugins for that extension point will be used if there is any.\n\t// If a QueueSort plugin is specified, the same QueueSort Plugin and\n\t// PluginConfig must be specified for all profiles.\n\tPlugins *Plugins `json:\"plugins,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PluginConfig is an optional set of custom plugin arguments for each plugin.\n\t// Omitting config args for a plugin is equivalent to using the default config\n\t// for that plugin.\n\t// +listType=map\n\t// +listMapKey=name\n\tPluginConfig []PluginConfig `json:\"pluginConfig,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// Plugins include multiple extension points. When specified, the list of plugins for\n// a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\n// omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\n// Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\n// be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\ntype Plugins struct {\n\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\n\tPreEnqueue PluginSet `json:\"preEnqueue,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\n\tQueueSort PluginSet `json:\"queueSort,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"PreFilter\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n\tPreFilter PluginSet `json:\"preFilter,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\n\tFilter PluginSet `json:\"filter,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\n\tPostFilter PluginSet `json:\"postFilter,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\n\tPreScore PluginSet `json:\"preScore,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\n\tScore PluginSet `json:\"score,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\n\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\n\tReserve PluginSet `json:\"reserve,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\n\tPermit PluginSet `json:\"permit,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\n\tPreBind PluginSet `json:\"preBind,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"Bind\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n\tBind PluginSet `json:\"bind,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n\tPostBind PluginSet `json:\"postBind,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config section to enable plugins for all valid extension points.\n\t// Plugins enabled through MultiPoint will automatically register for every individual extension\n\t// point the plugin has implemented. Disabling a plugin through MultiPoint disables that behavior.\n\t// The same is true for disabling \"*\" through MultiPoint (no default plugins will be automatically registered).\n\t// Plugins can still be disabled through their individual extension points.\n\t//\n\t// In terms of precedence, plugin config follows this basic hierarchy\n\t//   1. Specific extension points\n\t//   2. Explicitly configured MultiPoint plugins\n\t//   3. The set of default plugins, as MultiPoint plugins\n\t// This implies that a higher precedence plugin will run first and overwrite any settings within MultiPoint.\n\t// Explicitly user-configured plugins also take a higher precedence over default plugins.\n\t// Within this hierarchy, an Enabled setting takes precedence over Disabled. For example, if a plugin is\n\t// set in both `multiPoint.Enabled` and `multiPoint.Disabled`, the plugin will be enabled. Similarly,\n\t// including `multiPoint.Disabled = '*'` and `multiPoint.Enabled = pluginA` will still register that specific\n\t// plugin through MultiPoint. This follows the same behavior as all other extension point configurations.\n\tMultiPoint PluginSet `json:\"multiPoint,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\n// If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\ntype PluginSet struct {\n\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\n\t// If the default plugin is also configured in the scheduler config file, the weight of plugin will\n\t// be overridden accordingly.\n\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tEnabled []Plugin `json:\"enabled,omitempty\"`\n\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\n\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \"*\" should be provided.\n\t// +listType=map\n\t// +listMapKey=name\n\tDisabled []Plugin `json:\"disabled,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Weight is used only for Score plugins.\ntype Plugin struct {\n\t// Name defines the name of plugin\n\tName string `json:\"name\"`\n\t// Weight defines the weight of plugin, only used for Score plugins.\n\tWeight *int32 `json:\"weight,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// PluginConfig specifies arguments that should be passed to a plugin at the time of initialization.\n// A plugin that is invoked at multiple extension points is initialized once. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n// It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\ntype PluginConfig struct {\n\t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\n\tName string `json:\"name\"`\n\t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n\tArgs runtime.RawExtension `json:\"args,omitempty\"`\n}\n\nfunc (c *PluginConfig) decodeNestedObjects(d runtime.Decoder) error {\n\tgvk := SchemeGroupVersion.WithKind(c.Name + \"Args\")\n\t// dry-run to detect and skip out-of-tree plugin args.\n\tif _, _, err := d.Decode(nil, &gvk, nil); runtime.IsNotRegisteredError(err) {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tvar strictDecodingErr error\n\tobj, parsedGvk, err := d.Decode(c.Args.Raw, &gvk, nil)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tdecodingArgsErr := fmt.Errorf(\"decoding args for plugin %s: %w\", c.Name, err)\n\t\tif obj != nil && runtime.IsStrictDecodingError(err) {\n\t\t\tstrictDecodingErr = runtime.NewStrictDecodingError([]error{decodingArgsErr})\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\treturn decodingArgsErr\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif parsedGvk.GroupKind() != gvk.GroupKind() {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"args for plugin %s were not of type %s, got %s\", c.Name, gvk.GroupKind(), parsedGvk.GroupKind())\n\t}\n\tc.Args.Object = obj\n\treturn strictDecodingErr\n}\n\nfunc (c *PluginConfig) encodeNestedObjects(e runtime.Encoder) error {\n\tif c.Args.Object == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\terr := e.Encode(c.Args.Object, &buf)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\t// The <e> encoder might be a YAML encoder, but the parent encoder expects\n\t// JSON output, so we convert YAML back to JSON.\n\t// This is a no-op if <e> produces JSON.\n\tjson, err := yaml.YAMLToJSON(buf.Bytes())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tc.Args.Raw = json\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Extender holds the parameters used to communicate with the extender. If a verb is unspecified/empty,\n// it is assumed that the extender chose not to provide that extension.\ntype Extender struct {\n\t// URLPrefix at which the extender is available\n\tURLPrefix string `json:\"urlPrefix\"`\n\t// Verb for the filter call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the filter call to extender.\n\tFilterVerb string `json:\"filterVerb,omitempty\"`\n\t// Verb for the preempt call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the preempt call to extender.\n\tPreemptVerb string `json:\"preemptVerb,omitempty\"`\n\t// Verb for the prioritize call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the prioritize call to extender.\n\tPrioritizeVerb string `json:\"prioritizeVerb,omitempty\"`\n\t// The numeric multiplier for the node scores that the prioritize call generates.\n\t// The weight should be a positive integer\n\tWeight int64 `json:\"weight,omitempty\"`\n\t// Verb for the bind call, empty if not supported. This verb is appended to the URLPrefix when issuing the bind call to extender.\n\t// If this method is implemented by the extender, it is the extender's responsibility to bind the pod to apiserver. Only one extender\n\t// can implement this function.\n\tBindVerb string `json:\"bindVerb,omitempty\"`\n\t// EnableHTTPS specifies whether https should be used to communicate with the extender\n\tEnableHTTPS bool `json:\"enableHTTPS,omitempty\"`\n\t// TLSConfig specifies the transport layer security config\n\tTLSConfig *ExtenderTLSConfig `json:\"tlsConfig,omitempty\"`\n\t// HTTPTimeout specifies the timeout duration for a call to the extender. Filter timeout fails the scheduling of the pod. Prioritize\n\t// timeout is ignored, k8s/other extenders priorities are used to select the node.\n\tHTTPTimeout metav1.Duration `json:\"httpTimeout,omitempty\"`\n\t// NodeCacheCapable specifies that the extender is capable of caching node information,\n\t// so the scheduler should only send minimal information about the eligible nodes\n\t// assuming that the extender already cached full details of all nodes in the cluster\n\tNodeCacheCapable bool `json:\"nodeCacheCapable,omitempty\"`\n\t// ManagedResources is a list of extended resources that are managed by\n\t// this extender.\n\t// - A pod will be sent to the extender on the Filter, Prioritize and Bind\n\t//   (if the extender is the binder) phases iff the pod requests at least\n\t//   one of the extended resources in this list. If empty or unspecified,\n\t//   all pods will be sent to this extender.\n\t// - If IgnoredByScheduler is set to true for a resource, kube-scheduler\n\t//   will skip checking the resource in predicates.\n\t// +optional\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tManagedResources []ExtenderManagedResource `json:\"managedResources,omitempty\"`\n\t// Ignorable specifies if the extender is ignorable, i.e. scheduling should not\n\t// fail when the extender returns an error or is not reachable.\n\tIgnorable bool `json:\"ignorable,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// ExtenderManagedResource describes the arguments of extended resources\n// managed by an extender.\ntype ExtenderManagedResource struct {\n\t// Name is the extended resource name.\n\tName string `json:\"name\"`\n\t// IgnoredByScheduler indicates whether kube-scheduler should ignore this\n\t// resource when applying predicates.\n\tIgnoredByScheduler bool `json:\"ignoredByScheduler,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// ExtenderTLSConfig contains settings to enable TLS with extender\ntype ExtenderTLSConfig struct {\n\t// Server should be accessed without verifying the TLS certificate. For testing only.\n\tInsecure bool `json:\"insecure,omitempty\"`\n\t// ServerName is passed to the server for SNI and is used in the client to check server\n\t// certificates against. If ServerName is empty, the hostname used to contact the\n\t// server is used.\n\tServerName string `json:\"serverName,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// Server requires TLS client certificate authentication\n\tCertFile string `json:\"certFile,omitempty\"`\n\t// Server requires TLS client certificate authentication\n\tKeyFile string `json:\"keyFile,omitempty\"`\n\t// Trusted root certificates for server\n\tCAFile string `json:\"caFile,omitempty\"`\n\n\t// CertData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a client certificate file).\n\t// CertData takes precedence over CertFile\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tCertData []byte `json:\"certData,omitempty\"`\n\t// KeyData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a client certificate key file).\n\t// KeyData takes precedence over KeyFile\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tKeyData []byte `json:\"keyData,omitempty\"`\n\t// CAData holds PEM-encoded bytes (typically read from a root certificates bundle).\n\t// CAData takes precedence over CAFile\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tCAData []byte `json:\"caData,omitempty\"`\n}\n",
